Allah's Existence
beginner
5 min
Historical Observation of Worship's Benefits
The author argues from historical observation that devotion to God leads to worldly well-being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses historical observation as an inductive proof for the worldly benefits of devotion to God.

Core Idea
History shows: devotion to God leads to worldly well-being.

This lesson presents the second argument from the historians. It is an empirical argument based on patterns observed across history. The author claims that those more devoted to God enjoy better worldly conditions, while the worldly-minded suffer more. Let's examine the textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the author's claim sink in before analyzing.
Notice the parallel structure comparing two groups.
2
Identify the two historical patterns
The passage describes two findings: one about groups devoted to God, and another about those distant from God. Find the specific benefits and harms mentioned for each.
3
Understand the method of certainty
The author says certainty comes from long experience, reflection, and study of history. Ask: why is this important for the argument?
This is an inductive argument, not a logical proof.
4
Reflect on the argument's strength
Consider whether this historical correlation proves causation. The commentary will help clarify the author's intent.
The common misunderstanding warns against taking this as a guarantee for individuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثاني : من دلائل هذه الطائفة : أن أصحاب التواريخ لما بحثوا عن أحوال الدنيا وفتشوا عن أخبارها ، وجدوا أن كل طائفة كان تمسكهم بعبودية الله أشد ، وكان اشتغالهم بعبادة الله أكثر ، وكانت مواظبتهم على ذكر الله [ تعالى ] وعلى الفكرة في دلائل الله أكثر ؛ كانوا في الدنيا أحسن ذكرا ، وأطول أعماراً ، وأكثر خيراً ونعمة، وأبعد عن الشرور ، والآفات ، وأقرب إلى دوام الخيرات والسعادات. وكل من كان أبعد عن طاعة الله ، وأكثر استغراقا في طلب الدنيا وحبها ، كانوا إلى الهلاك والشرور أقرب ، وإلى الوقوع في الآفات والمخافات أوصل . وهذه أحوال لا يعرفها إلا من طالت تجربته في أحوال أهل الدنيا ، وكثرت فكرته في كيفية أحوالهم ، وطالع أيضاً كتب التواريخ ، وعرف أحوال الماضين من المقرين والمنكرين ، فإنه يقطع بعد التجربة التي ذكرناها وبعد الأفكار التي أرشدنا إليها : أن الأمر كما ذكرناه ، وأنه لا شبهة في حقيقة ما ادعيناه .
And the second aspect of the proofs of this group: that the historians, when they researched the conditions of the world and investigated its reports, found that every group that had a stronger adherence to the worship of God, and was more engaged in the worship of God, and was more constant in the remembrance of God Almighty and in reflection upon the proofs of God, they were in the world of better reputation, longer lives, more abundant in good and blessing, more distant from evils and afflictions, and closer to the permanence of good things and happiness. And everyone who was more distant from obedience to God, and more immersed in seeking the world and loving it, they were closer to destruction and evils, and more likely to fall into afflictions and fears. And these are conditions that only one whose experience with the conditions of the people of the world has been long, and whose reflection on the nature of their conditions has been abundant, and who has also studied history books and known the conditions of the past, both those who affirmed and those who denied—he will be certain, after the experience we have mentioned and after the reflections we have guided to, that the matter is as we have stated, and that there is no doubt about the truth of what we have claimed.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage presents the second argument from the group (the historians). It is an empirical argument based on historical observation. The author states that historians have consistently found a correlation: those who are more devoted to God—through stronger adherence to worship, more engagement in worship, and more remembrance and reflection—enjoy better worldly conditions: better reputation, longer lives, more blessings, and fewer evils. Conversely, those who are distant from God and absorbed in worldliness suffer more destruction and affliction. The author emphasizes that this conclusion is reached only after extensive experience, reflection, and study of history, leading to certainty. The argument is thus based on repeated historical patterns, making it a form of inductive proof.

Key Terms
عبادة
ذكر
تجربة
تواريخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think this argument guarantees worldly success for every individual believer.
Correction: The author speaks in terms of general historical patterns and group tendencies, not individual cases.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did historians find about groups that were more devoted to God?
A) They suffered more afflictions.
B) They had shorter lives.
C) They had better reputation and longer lives.
D) They were ignored in history.

Key Takeaway
Historical observation reveals a consistent pattern: devotion to God leads to worldly well-being, while distance from God leads to misfortune.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you honestly examine your own life, do you see a correlation between your devotion to God and your inner peace and outer well-being? Where have you personally experienced this pattern, and where have you seen it falter? What does that reveal about your relationship with Allah? Commit to a week of increased worship and reflection, and journal the effects.
?
The author says that only those who have reflected deeply on history and their own experience can be certain of this truth. Have you ever taken time to reflect on your own life's history of obedience and its outcomes? If not, what is stopping you? Start today by recalling a specific moment when drawing close to God brought you a tangible good, and use it to strengthen your faith.
?
This argument uses history to prove God's existence, but it also serves as a personal warning. Are you more like the groups devoted to God or those distant from Him when you examine your daily pursuits? What small change can you make starting tomorrow to increase your 'adherence to the worship of God' and decrease your immersion in worldly distractions?

Four Supporting Points Strengthening the Historical Argument
The author lists four supporting observations for the historical argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four observations that strengthen the historical argument for divine existence based on patterns of worldly success and durability.

Core Idea
Piety correlates with worldly success and endurance, reinforcing the historical argument.

The author previously presented a historical argument based on the benefits of devotion. Here, he offers four specific observations that add weight to that argument. These points draw on common historical patterns, showing that religious dedication brings both inner and outer rewards. Read closely to see how each observation builds a cumulative case.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Notice the clear enumeration of four points.
The author uses 'الأول', 'الثاني', etc. to structure the points.
2
Identify each observation
For each of the four points, state in your own words what historical pattern the author is highlighting.
3
Connect each point to the argument
Ask yourself: how does this observation support the idea that there is a wise and just God who rewards piety?
Consider the contrast between pious and impious outcomes.
4
Reflect on the cumulative force
Think about how these four independent patterns together strengthen the historical argument. Why would the author present them as a list?
The strength lies in the convergence of evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يقوى ذلك وجوه : الأول : إن وقوع الظلمة ، وطلاب الدنيا في أنواع القتل والنهب ، أكثر من وقوع أهل العلم والعمل ، في تلك الآفات . الثاني : إن المدرسة الحقيرة [ المبنية] لأهل العلم ، والرباط الحقير المبني لأهل الطاعة قد يبقى مائتي سنة أو ثلثمائة سنة ، وأما القصور العالية ، والأبنية المشيدة التي للملوك ، فإنها لا تبقى إلا زماناً قليلاً ، وذلك يدل على ما قلناه . الثالث : إن باني المدارس والرباطات ، كلما كان أقرب إلى الدين والطاعة ، كانت أبنيته أبقي . الرابع : إن ذكر أهل العلم وأهل الدين أبقى من ذكر الظلمة وأهل الشر.
And among what strengthens that are aspects: The first: that the occurrence of oppressors and seekers of the world in types of killing and plunder is more than the occurrence of people of knowledge and action in those afflictions. The second: that the humble school built for people of knowledge, and the humble hospice built for people of obedience, may remain for two hundred or three hundred years, while the lofty palaces and fortified buildings of kings remain only a short time. And that indicates what we have said. The third: that the builder of schools and hospices, the closer he is to religion and obedience, the more enduring his buildings are. The fourth: that the remembrance of the people of knowledge and the people of religion is more lasting than the remembrance of oppressors and people of evil.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage lists four supporting points that strengthen the previous historical argument about the benefits of devotion. The first point: oppressors and worldly people suffer more from violence than the pious. The second: humble religious buildings (schools and hospices) often last for centuries, while grand palaces of kings quickly decay. The third: the more pious the builder, the more enduring his buildings. The fourth: the reputation of scholars and religious people outlasts that of tyrants and evildoers. Each of these observations reinforces the idea that piety is associated with worldly and historical success, supporting the existence of a just and wise God.

Key Terms
ظلمة
مدرسة
رباط
ذكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These observations are just isolated anecdotes without general validity.
Correction: The author presents them as general historical patterns observed by historians, not mere anecdotes.

Checkpoint
According to the third supporting point, what factor determines how enduring a building is?
A) The wealth of the builder.
B) The size of the building.
C) The piety of the builder.
D) The location of the building.

Key Takeaway
The four observations cumulatively show that piety leads to greater worldly and historical success, strengthening the argument for divine existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your life were measured by the four observations—protection from harm, longevity of your works, endurance of what you build, and lasting remembrance—which of these would you feel confident about? What does your answer reveal about the distance between your current priorities and the path of piety?
?
The humble school and hospice remain for centuries while the palaces of kings crumble. What are you investing your time, energy, and resources in? Are you building temporary palaces for yourself or enduring structures for the sake of Allah?
?
Allah has made the remembrance of the people of knowledge and religion outlast that of oppressors. Will you be remembered for your devotion to truth or for worldly pursuits? Starting today, what one concrete step will you take to align your legacy with the people of knowledge?

The Historical Pattern of Devotion and Worldly Success
Sanusi presents his historical observation about the worldly outcomes of the devout versus the worldly.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses historical observation to establish a correlation between devotion to God and worldly well-being.

Core Idea
History shows that the devout flourish, while the worldly perish.

The author begins by inviting us to examine the conditions of societies throughout history. He claims that a clear pattern emerges: those who are more devoted to God enjoy better lives, while those who are absorbed in worldly pursuits suffer more. This observation forms the basis of his empirical argument for the existence of a wise God.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening observation
Read the first part of the passage where the author describes the pattern he has observed about devout vs. worldly people.
Notice the list of benefits: better reputation, longer life, more good, etc.
2
Understand the condition of the worldly
The author contrasts with those who are distant from obedience, noting their proximity to destruction.
3
Recognize the source of this knowledge
The author states this is known only through long experience and study of history.
This emphasizes the empirical nature of the proof.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that there is no doubt about this pattern.
This sets up the need for further proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن أحوال الدنيا وفتشوا عن أخبارها ، وجدوا أن كل طائفة كان تمسكهم بعبودية الله أشد ، وكان اشتغالهم بعبادة الله أكثر ، وكانت مواظبتهم على ذكر الله [ تعالى ] وعلى الفكرة في دلائل الله أكثر ؛ كانوا في الدنيا أحسن ذكرا ، وأطول أعماراً ، وأكثر خيراً ونعمة، وأبعد عن الشرور ، والآفات ، وأقرب إلى دوام الخيرات والسعادات. وكل من كان أبعد عن طاعة الله ، وأكثر استغراقا في طلب الدنيا وحبها ، كانوا إلى الهلاك والشرور أقرب ، وإلى الوقوع في الآفات والمخافات أوصل . وهذه أحوال لا يعرفها إلا من طالت تجربته في أحوال أهل الدنيا ، وكثرت فكرته في كيفية أحوالهم ، وطالع أيضاً كتب التواريخ ، وعرف أحوال الماضين من المقرين والمنكرين ، فإنه يقطع بعد التجربة التي ذكرناها وبعد الأفكار التي أرشدنا إليها : أن الأمر كما ذكرناه ، وأنه لا شبهة في حقيقة ما ادعيناه . ومما يقوى ذلك وجوه : الأول : إن وقوع الظلمة ، وطلاب الدنيا في أنواع القتل والنهب ، أكثر من وقوع أهل العلم والعمل ، في تلك الآفات . الثاني : إن المدرسة الحقيرة [ المبنية] لأهل العلم ، والرباط الحقير المبني لأهل الطاعة قد يبقى مائتي سنة أو ثلثمائة سنة ، وأما القصور العالية ، والأبنية المشيدة التي للملوك ، فإنها لا تبقى إلا زماناً قليلاً ، وذلك يدل على ما قلناه . الثالث : إن باني المدارس والرباطات ، كلما كان أقرب إلى الدين والطاعة ، كانت أبنيته أبقي . الرابع : إن ذكر أهل العلم وأهل الدين أبقى من ذكر الظلمة وأهل الشر . الخامس : إن ميل القلوب إلى أهل الدين والطاعة ، أكثر من ميلها إلى أهل الدنيا ، وكل ذلك يدل على أن كل من كان أوغل في عبودية الله ، كان أقرب إلى الخيرات ، ولما رأينا بحسب هذه التجربة أن الإقرار بالإلهية ، والاعتراف بوجوب الطاعة والخدمة، كمال السعادات في الدنيا . فهذا من أدل الدلائل على وجود الإله الرحيم الحكيم . وهذا النوع من الدلائل كثير في القرآن العظيم . قال الله تعالى : ( لقد كان في قصصهم عبرة لأولي الألباب ) وقال : « كم تركوا من جنات وعيون) إلى قوله : ( فما بكت عليهم السماء والأرض ، وما كانوا منظرين ) . وبالجملة : فلما دلت المشاهدة والتجربة على أن الاعتراف بهذه المعاني سبب لانفتاح أبواب السعادات [ والإعراض عنها سبب لانفتاح أبواب الآفات ] علمنا أن الطريق الحق والمنهج الصدق هو الإقرار بوجود الإله الحكيم الرحيم . فهذا هو الإشارة إلى الدلائل المستنبطة من علم التواريخ على وجود الإله لهذا العالم .
Regarding the conditions of the world and if they investigate its reports, they find that every group whose hold on the worship of God was stronger, and whose occupation with worshipping God was greater, and whose diligence in remembering God (Exalted be He) and in reflecting upon the proofs of God was more, they were in the world better in reputation, longer in lifespan, more abundant in good and blessing, further from evils and afflictions, and nearer to the continuity of good things and happiness. And whoever was further from obedience to God and more immersed in seeking the world and loving it, they were closer to destruction and evils, and more likely to fall into afflictions and fears. These are conditions that only one whose experience in the conditions of worldly people is long, whose thought about the nature of their conditions is plentiful, and who has also perused historical books and known the conditions of past people, both those who affirmed and those who denied, knows; then he will decide after the experience we mentioned and after the thoughts we guided to that the matter is as we stated, and that there is no doubt in the reality of what we claim. And among what strengthens that are [several] aspects: First: The occurrence of oppressors and seekers of the world in types of killing and plunder is more than the occurrence of people of knowledge and action in those afflictions. Second: The humble school built for people of knowledge and the humble lodge built for people of obedience may remain two hundred years or three hundred years, whereas the high palaces and lofty buildings of kings do not remain except a short time, and that indicates what we said. Third: The builder of schools and lodges, the closer he is to religion and obedience, the more lasting his buildings are. Fourth: The remembrance of people of knowledge and people of religion is more lasting than the remembrance of oppressors and people of evil. Fifth: The inclination of hearts towards people of religion and obedience is greater than their inclination towards people of the world. And all that indicates that whoever is more immersed in the worship of God is closer to good things. And since we have seen according to this experience that affirming divinity and acknowledging the obligation of obedience and service is the perfection of happiness in this world, this is among the strongest proofs for the existence of the Merciful, Wise God. And this type of proof is abundant in the Mighty Quran. God Almighty said: 'Indeed in their stories is a lesson for those of understanding' (Yusuf 12:111) and said: 'How many gardens and springs they left behind...' until His saying: 'And the heaven and earth wept not for them, nor were they reprieved' (al-Dukhan 44:25-29). And in summary: Since observation and experience have indicated that acknowledging these meanings is a cause for opening the doors of happiness, and turning away from them is a cause for opening the doors of afflictions, we know that the correct path and the truthful way is affirming the existence of the Wise, Merciful God. This is the indication to the proofs derived from the science of history for the existence of God for this world.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage presents an empirical-historical argument for the existence of God, based on observing the worldly conditions of those who are devout versus those who are worldly. The author begins by stating a general observation: those who are more devoted to God enjoy better reputations, longer lives, more blessings, and fewer afflictions in this world. Conversely, those who are more absorbed in worldly pursuits are closer to destruction and evil. This pattern is known only through long experience and study of history. The author then provides five specific proofs (وجوه) that strengthen this observation. First: oppressors and worldly people suffer more from killing and plunder than righteous scholars. Second: humble schools and lodges for worship last for centuries, while grand royal palaces decay quickly. Third: the more religious the builder, the more lasting his building. Fourth: the memory of religious people endures longer than that of oppressors. Fifth: hearts incline more towards religious people than worldly people. All these point to the principle that deeper devotion to God brings greater good. Since acknowledging God and obeying Him leads to worldly happiness, this is a strong indication of the existence of a Merciful, Wise God. The author then cites Quranic verses as additional evidence, concluding that observation and experience confirm that affirming God is the path to happiness, thus proving His existence.

Key Terms
تجربة
مشاهدة
تواريخ
عبودية
سعادات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author's argument is purely logical and deductive, not based on experience.
Correction: The author explicitly grounds his proof in empirical observation and historical study, not abstract reasoning.

Checkpoint
What does the author say is required to know the conditions he describes?
A) A strong intellect
B) Long experience and study of history
C) Blind faith
D) Divine revelation

Key Takeaway
Historical observation reveals a consistent pattern: devotion to God correlates with worldly flourishing, and worldliness correlates with worldly ruin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you honestly assess your current priorities, are you more immersed in 'seeking the world and loving it' or in 'holding onto worship of God'? What specific evidence from your past month supports your answer? Write down one concrete change you will make tonight to tip the balance toward devotion.
?
Sanusi says that those who reflect on history and their own experience will be certain. Have you ever truly observed this pattern in your own life or in the lives of people around you? If not, what might be blocking your vision? Commit to spend 10 minutes tonight recalling two examples of this pattern from people you know—one of devotion leading to blessing and one of worldliness leading to ruin.
?
The passage warns that worldliness leads to 'destruction and evils' and 'afflictions and fears'. Is there any area of your life where you are clinging to worldly attainment while neglecting obedience to God? Name it. What is your next step to repent and return to servitude? Be specific.

Five Empirical Proofs Supporting the Historical Argument
Sanusi enumerates five empirical proofs and concludes that acknowledging God leads to happiness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five specific proofs the author gives to strengthen his historical observation.

Core Idea
Five observable facts confirm that devotion to God brings worldly benefits.

The author follows his general observation with five concrete proofs that anyone can examine. These proofs range from the durability of buildings to the inclination of human hearts. Each proof reinforces the central thesis that closeness to God leads to worldly good.

Guided Path
1
Read the five proofs
Read the list of five proofs carefully. They are numbered in the text.
Each proof is a distinct observation.
2
Analyze each proof
For each proof, identify the comparison being made and how it supports the claim that devotion leads to good.
Proof 1: oppressors vs. scholars. Proof 2: religious buildings vs. royal palaces. Proof 3: builder's piety and building durability. Proof 4: lasting remembrance. Proof 5: heart inclination.
3
Understand the cumulative argument
The author says all these together indicate that deeper devotion leads to greater good.
He then concludes that acknowledging God is the path to happiness.
4
Connect to the conclusion
The author concludes that observation and experience prove the existence of a Wise, Merciful God.
He cites Quranic verses as support.

الرابع : إن ذكر أهل العلم وأهل الدين أبقى من ذكر الظلمة وأهل الشر . الخامس : إن ميل القلوب إلى أهل الدين والطاعة ، أكثر من ميلها إلى أهل الدنيا ، وكل ذلك يدل على أن كل من كان أوغل في عبودية الله ، كان أقرب إلى الخيرات ، ولما رأينا بحسب هذه التجربة أن الإقرار بالإلهية ، والاعتراف بوجوب الطاعة والخدمة، كمال السعادات في الدنيا . فهذا من أدل الدلائل على وجود الإله الرحيم الحكيم . وهذا النوع من الدلائل كثير في القرآن العظيم . قال الله تعالى : ( لقد كان في قصصهم عبرة لأولي الألباب ) وقال : « كم تركوا من جنات وعيون) إلى قوله : ( فما بكت عليهم السماء والأرض ، وما كانوا منظرين ) . وبالجملة : فلما دلت المشاهدة والتجربة على أن الاعتراف بهذه المعاني سبب لانفتاح أبواب السعادات [ والإعراض عنها سبب لانفتاح أبواب الآفات ] علمنا أن الطريق الحق والمنهج الصدق هو الإقرار بوجود الإله الحكيم الرحيم . فهذا هو الإشارة إلى الدلائل المستنبطة من علم التواريخ على وجود الإله لهذا العالم .
Regarding the conditions of the world and if they investigate its reports, they find that every group whose hold on the worship of God was stronger, and whose occupation with worshipping God was greater, and whose diligence in remembering God (Exalted be He) and in reflecting upon the proofs of God was more, they were in the world better in reputation, longer in lifespan, more abundant in good and blessing, further from evils and afflictions, and nearer to the continuity of good things and happiness. And whoever was further from obedience to God and more immersed in seeking the world and loving it, they were closer to destruction and evils, and more likely to fall into afflictions and fears. These are conditions that only one whose experience in the conditions of worldly people is long, whose thought about the nature of their conditions is plentiful, and who has also perused historical books and known the conditions of past people, both those who affirmed and those who denied, knows; then he will decide after the experience we mentioned and after the thoughts we guided to that the matter is as we stated, and that there is no doubt in the reality of what we claim. And among what strengthens that are [several] aspects: First: The occurrence of oppressors and seekers of the world in types of killing and plunder is more than the occurrence of people of knowledge and action in those afflictions. Second: The humble school built for people of knowledge and the humble lodge built for people of obedience may remain two hundred years or three hundred years, whereas the high palaces and lofty buildings of kings do not remain except a short time, and that indicates what we said. Third: The builder of schools and lodges, the closer he is to religion and obedience, the more lasting his buildings are. Fourth: The remembrance of people of knowledge and people of religion is more lasting than the remembrance of oppressors and people of evil. Fifth: The inclination of hearts towards people of religion and obedience is greater than their inclination towards people of the world. And all that indicates that whoever is more immersed in the worship of God is closer to good things. And since we have seen according to this experience that affirming divinity and acknowledging the obligation of obedience and service is the perfection of happiness in this world, this is among the strongest proofs for the existence of the Merciful, Wise God. And this type of proof is abundant in the Mighty Quran. God Almighty said: 'Indeed in their stories is a lesson for those of understanding' (Yusuf 12:111) and said: 'How many gardens and springs they left behind...' until His saying: 'And the heaven and earth wept not for them, nor were they reprieved' (al-Dukhan 44:25-29). And in summary: Since observation and experience have indicated that acknowledging these meanings is a cause for opening the doors of happiness, and turning away from them is a cause for opening the doors of afflictions, we know that the correct path and the truthful way is affirming the existence of the Wise, Merciful God. This is the indication to the proofs derived from the science of history for the existence of God for this world.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage presents an empirical-historical argument for the existence of God, based on observing the worldly conditions of those who are devout versus those who are worldly. The author begins by stating a general observation: those who are more devoted to God enjoy better reputations, longer lives, more blessings, and fewer afflictions in this world. Conversely, those who are more absorbed in worldly pursuits are closer to destruction and evil. This pattern is known only through long experience and study of history. The author then provides five specific proofs (وجوه) that strengthen this observation. First: oppressors and worldly people suffer more from killing and plunder than righteous scholars. Second: humble schools and lodges for worship last for centuries, while grand royal palaces decay quickly. Third: the more religious the builder, the more lasting his building. Fourth: the memory of religious people endures longer than that of oppressors. Fifth: hearts incline more towards religious people than worldly people. All these point to the principle that deeper devotion to God brings greater good. Since acknowledging God and obeying Him leads to worldly happiness, this is a strong indication of the existence of a Merciful, Wise God. The author then cites Quranic verses as additional evidence, concluding that observation and experience confirm that affirming God is the path to happiness, thus proving His existence.

Key Terms
وجوه
ظلمة
مدرسة
رباط
ذکر
ميل القلوب

Checkpoint

A) The longevity of religious buildings vs. royal palaces
B) The lifespan of religious people vs. worldly people
C) The number of oppressors vs. scholars
D) The inclination of hearts

Key Takeaway
The five empirical proofs cumulatively demonstrate that devotion to God correlates with worldly good, pointing to the existence of a Wise, Merciful God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The source says that 'acknowledging divinity and the obligation of obedience' is the perfection of happiness in this world. Are you truly acknowledging God in your daily decisions, or are you still chasing worldly pursuits that the first proof warns fade? What is one concrete step you can take today to align your life more with devotion?
?
If you were to die today, would your life be more like the lasting remembrance of the righteous or the forgotten legacy of the oppressors? How does that question make you feel, and what change does it demand from you starting now?

Classification of Existents into Corporeal and Spiritual
The author classifies all existents into three types and groups them into corporeal and spiritual.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational classification of all existents into corporeal and spiritual, and how this division underpins arguments for God's existence.

Core Idea
All existents are either corporeal or spiritual—a foundational division in rational theology.

This passage from the second group of spiritual practitioners presents a rational classification of beings. Reason observes three categories: bodies, their attributes, and that which is neither. The first two are grouped as corporeal, the last as spiritual. This simple division is crucial because it establishes the reality of non-physical existence, opening the door to proofs for a transcendent Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic once, then the translation. Notice the author's claim that reason witnesses this division.
The passage begins a new section on proofs from spiritual discipline.
2
Identify the three divisions
Find the three categories listed: bodies, attributes of bodies, and what is neither body nor state in a body. Understand what each means.
Attributes include all accidents; the third is the spiritual realm.
3
Understand the two-fold grouping
See how the first two are called 'corporeal' and the third 'spiritual'. This yields the final classification.
This grouping is based on physical vs. non-physical.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask why this classification matters for proving God. It shows that there are non-material realities, allowing for a non-material Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطائفة الثانية : طوائف أصحاب الرياضيات وأرباب المكاشفات : واعلم أن طريقهم يدل على وجود الإله الحكيم الرحيم من أنواع : النوع الأول : أن نقول : إن صريح العقل شاهد بأن الموجودات على ثلاثة أقسام : الأجسام ، وصفات الأجسام ، والذي لا يكون جسماً ولا حالا في الجسم . أما القسمان الأولان فهما اللذان يسميان الجسمانيات . وأما القسم الأخير : فهو المسمى بالروحانيات ، فثبت بهذا التقسيم : أن الموجودات إما جسمانية ، وإما روحانية.
The second group: the groups of practitioners of spiritual disciplines and people of unveilings. Know that their way indicates the existence of the Wise, Merciful God through [several] types. The first type: that we say: Verily, clear reason witnesses that existents are of three divisions: bodies, attributes of bodies, and that which is neither a body nor a state in a body. As for the first two divisions, they are those called corporeals. And as for the last division, it is what is called spirituals. So it is established by this division that existents are either corporeal or spiritual.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on the second group of people who seek knowledge of God: the practitioners of spiritual disciplines (رياضيات) and those who experience unveilings (مكاشفات). The author states that their path provides proofs for God's existence, and he begins with the first type of proof: a rational classification of all existents. According to reason, beings fall into three categories: bodies (أجسام), which are extended substances; attributes of bodies (صفات الأجسام), which are accidents or qualities inhering in bodies; and that which is neither a body nor a state in a body (لا يكون جسماً ولا حالا في الجسم), which is the spiritual realm. The first two are grouped together as 'corporeal' (جسمانيات), while the third is 'spiritual' (روحانيات). This two-fold division into corporeal and spiritual is the foundation for further arguments, because it establishes that there are non-physical realities, which then allows for proofs of a non-physical Creator.

Key Terms

المكاشفات
الأجسام

الجسمانيات
الروحانيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think 'صفات الأجسام' refers only to essential attributes and not accidental qualities.
Correction: In fact, it includes all accidents and qualities that inhere in bodies, not just essential attributes.

Checkpoint

B) Attributes of bodies
C) Accidents

Key Takeaway
Existents are rationally divided into corporeal and spiritual, with the spiritual being that which is neither a body nor an accident.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If your soul is a spiritual being, not a body or an accident, then what does that mean for how you treat it compared to your physical desires?
?
When you look at your daily worries, do they mostly belong to the corporeal or the spiritual realm? What would shift if you gave more weight to the spiritual?

The Fifth Proof: Empirical Observation of Hearts Inclining to Religion
Al-Razi presents the fifth proof for God's existence based on empirical observation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how empirical observation of human inclinations serves as a proof for God's existence, as presented by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi.

Core Idea
Human hearts naturally prefer the religious over the worldly—this universal experience points to God.

Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents a unique proof for God's existence based not on abstract logic but on observable human behavior. He argues that across societies, people's hearts incline more toward the devout than the worldly, indicating that devotion to God leads to true happiness. This passage connects this empirical observation to Quranic stories and historical evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how al-Razi presents the proof in a flowing argument, not in a numbered list.
The proof is based on a simple observation: people naturally admire the religious.
2
Identify the empirical observation
Al-Razi claims that hearts incline more to people of religion and obedience than to people of worldly pursuits. This is the foundation of the proof.
Think about your own experience: do you find yourself respecting devout people more than purely worldly ones?
3
Understand the reasoning from observation to conclusion
Al-Razi argues that if devotion to God leads to good things (as observed), then affirming God's existence and serving Him is the path to happiness. This proves a Merciful, Wise God exists.
The proof is inductive: from repeated experience to a general truth.
4
Reflect on the Quranic support
Al-Razi cites two Quranic verses that show how past nations' stories serve as lessons, and how the wicked were destroyed without heaven or earth mourning them. These support the idea that acknowledging God leads to happiness.
The Quran itself invites us to observe and learn from history.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : إن ميل القلوب إلى أهل الدين، والطاعة ، أكثر من ميلها إلى أهل الدنيا ، وكل ذلك يدل على أن كل من كان أوغل في عبودية الله ، كان أقرب إلى الخيرات ، ولما رأينا بحسب هذه التجربة أن الإقرار بالإلهية ، والاعتراف بوجوب الطاعة والخدمة، كمال السعادات في الدنيا . فهذا من أدل الدلائل على وجود الإله الرحيم الحكيم . وهذا النوع من الدلائل كثير في القرآن العظيم . قال الله تعالى : ( لقد كان في قصصهم عبرة لأولي الألباب ) (١) وقال : « كم تركوا من جنات وعيون) إلى قوله : ( فما بكت عليهم السماء والأرض ، ومــا كــانــوا منظرين ) (٢). وبالجملة : فلما دلت المشاهدة والتجربة على أن الاعتراف بهذه المعاني سبب لانفتاح أبواب السعادات [ والإعراض عنها سبب لانفتاح أبواب الآفات ] (٣) علمنا أن الطريق الحق والمنهج الصدق هو الإقرار بوجود الإله الحكيم الرحيم . فهذا هو الإشارة إلى الدلائل المستنبطة من علم التواريخ على وجود الإله لهذا العالم
Fifth: That the inclination of hearts to the people of religion and obedience is greater than their inclination to the people of this world, and all of that indicates that whoever is more deeply engaged in the worship of God is closer to good things. And since we have seen, according to this experience, that affirming divinity and acknowledging the obligation of obedience and service is the perfection of happiness in this world, this is among the strongest proofs for the existence of the Merciful, Wise God. And this kind of proof is abundant in the Mighty Quran. Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed in their stories is a lesson for those of understanding' (12:111) and said: 'How many gardens and springs they left behind' up to His saying: 'So the heaven and earth did not weep for them, nor were they reprieved' (44:25-29). In summary: Since observation and experience have shown that acknowledgment of these meanings is a cause for the opening of the doors of happiness, and turning away from them is a cause for the opening of the doors of afflictions, we know that the true path and the truthful way is the affirmation of the existence of the Wise, Merciful God. This is the indication to the proofs derived from the science of histories on the existence of the God of this world.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from empirical observation and historical experience. The author begins by stating the observation: hearts naturally incline more toward religious and obedient people than toward worldly people. This empirical fact indicates that those who are deeper in God's worship are closer to good things. The author then reflects on this experience, noting that affirming divinity and acknowledging the obligation of obedience and service constitutes the perfection of happiness in this world. Thus, this serves as a strong proof for the existence of a Merciful and Wise God. He supports this with Quranic verses that recount stories of past nations as lessons, and a verse describing how heaven and earth did not mourn the destruction of the wicked. The conclusion is that observation and experience confirm that acknowledging these meanings brings happiness, while turning away brings afflictions. Therefore, the correct path is to affirm the existence of the Wise and Merciful God. This type of proof is abundant in the Quran and derived from the science of histories.

Classification of Existents into Bodily and Spiritual
Al-Razi classifies existents into bodily and spiritual via a threefold division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational threefold classification of existents and how it leads to the affirmation of spiritual entities as higher than bodily ones.

Core Idea
All existents are bodily or spiritual; the spiritual are higher by nature.

This passage from al-Razi presents a foundational argument from the mathematicians and mystics. It begins with a clear rational classification of all existents into three categories, then groups them into bodily and spiritual. The author then appeals to the innate disposition (fitra) of rational people to affirm the existence and superiority of spiritual realities. Understanding this classification is essential for following the subsequent proofs for God's existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the author's logical flow sink in.
Notice the three distinct divisions presented in the first sentence.
2
Identify the three divisions
The passage lists three kinds of existents: bodies, attributes of bodies, and that which is neither a body nor an accident. Understand each category.
The first two are grouped as 'bodily things', the third as 'spiritual things'.
3
Understand the fitra claim
Al-Razi asserts that the innate nature of all complete rational beings testifies that spiritual existents exist and are superior. Reflect on what this means for the argument.
This is a claim about universal human intuition, not yet a proof.
4
Connect to the bigger picture
This classification sets the stage for arguments that God, as a spiritual existent, must exist. Consider how this classification supports that goal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطائفة الثانية : طوائف أصحاب الرياضيات وأرباب المكاشفات : واعلم أن طريقهم يدل على وجود الإله الحكيم الرحيم من أنواع : النوع الأول : أن نقول : إن صريح العقل شاهد بأن الموجودات على ثلاثة أقسام : الأجسام ، وصفات الأجسام ، والذي لا يكون جسماً ولا حالا في الجسم . أما القسمان الأولان فهما اللذان يسميان الجسمانيات . وأما القسم الأخير : فهو المسمى بالروحانيات ، فثبت بهذا التقسيم : أن الموجودات إما جسمانية ، وإما روحانية. إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : إن فطرة جميع العقلاء الكاملين تشهد بأن الموجودات الروحانية موجودة . وأنها مع كونها موجودة فهي أعلى، وأكمل وأشرف من الموجودات الجسمانية
The second group: The groups of the practitioners of mathematics and the masters of illuminations. Know that their path indicates the existence of the Wise, Merciful God through types. The first type: That we say: Indeed, clear reason witnesses that existents are of three divisions: bodies, the attributes of bodies, and that which is neither a body nor an accident in a body. As for the first two divisions, they are what are called bodily things. As for the last division, it is called spiritual things. So it is established by this division that existents are either bodily or spiritual. If you have understood this, then we say: The innate nature (fitra) of all complete rational beings testifies that spiritual existents exist, and that while they exist, they are higher, more perfect, and nobler than bodily existents.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage introduces the second group of proofs, attributed to mathematicians and mystics. The author states that their method establishes the existence of the Wise, Merciful God through several types. The first type begins with a rational classification: reason witnesses that existents are of three kinds—bodies, attributes of bodies (accidents), and that which is neither a body nor an accident (i.e., purely spiritual substances). The first two categories are together called 'bodily things' (jismaniyyat), and the third is called 'spiritual things' (ruhaniyyat). Thus, all existents are either bodily or spiritual. Having established this division, the author then makes a claim based on innate nature (fitra): the fitra of all complete rational people testifies that spiritual existents exist, and moreover that they are higher, more perfect, and nobler than bodily existents. This sets up the need for proofs, which follow in the subsequent text.

الأجسام
صفات الأجسام
الجسمانيات
الروحانيات
فطرة
العقلاء الكاملين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that only bodily things are real, or that spiritual things are imaginary or less real.
Correction: The passage affirms that spiritual existents are real and even higher, more perfect, and nobler than bodily existents, based on reason and innate human nature.

Checkpoint

B) Only bodies.
C) That which is neither a body nor an accident in a body.

Key Takeaway
The rational threefold division of existents leads to the conclusion that there are spiritual realities, which our innate nature confirms to be higher than material ones.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What concrete step can you take today to reawaken that innate recognition of the spiritual realm?
?

If you truly believed this hierarchy, how would your schedule, spending, and priorities change? Will you commit to one specific action this week that honors the spiritual over the bodily?
?
God is described in this classification as neither a body nor an accident. Do you ever catch yourself thinking of God in human-like or spatial terms? How can you actively purify your concept of God based on this rational division, and what difference would that make in your worship and trust in Him?

Proof from Hierarchy of Perfection
Proof of God's existence from hierarchy of perfection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hierarchy of perfection in both physical and spiritual beings leads to the rational necessity of a single, absolutely perfect being who is God.

Core Idea
Perfection exists in degrees; the highest must be God.

This passage presents a profound argument that moves from observable hierarchies in the world—first among human beings, then among spiritual beings—to the necessary existence of one ultimate perfect being. By reflecting on the limited perfection in creation, we are led to affirm a source of unlimited perfection, which is God. Follow the reasoning step by step to see how this argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three attributes of perfection
Read the first part where the author defines perfection in terms of three attributes: self-sufficiency, knowledge, and power. Notice that these are limited in human beings.
These three attributes are the yardstick for measuring perfection throughout the argument.
2
Trace the hierarchy in the physical world
The author describes how among humans, there is a gradation leading to one most perfect individual per era (the Pole or Imam), and ultimately a supreme prophet across time. Understand this as an observed fact.
This establishes that physical beings have a chain of dependence for perfection.
3
Apply the same reasoning to spiritual beings
Now the author asks you to consider spiritual beings (pure souls). They are more perfect than humans, yet they too exist in degrees. By analogy, there must be one most perfect spiritual being.
This being must be independent and the source of all perfections for others.
4
Conclude to the necessary being
The argument concludes that the most perfect spiritual being is completely independent and all others depend on Him. This being is God. Notice how the reasoning moves from contingent hierarchical perfection to a necessary self-sufficient being.
The conclusion is that the only being worthy of being called God is that one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل من كانت الجسمانية عليه أغلب ، كان أخس وأبعد من الكمال . ثم لما تأملنا في ضبط صفات الكمال ، وجدناها محصورة في ثلاثة أنواع : الاستغناء ، والعلم ، والقدرة . ثم من المعلوم أن هذه الصفات الثلاثة لا تحصل للإنسان على سبيل الكمال ، بل إنما تحصل له بمقدار القوة البشرية والطاقة الإنسانية . فنشاهد أن أصناف أهل العالم ، وإن كانوا كثيرين إلا أن (۱) الصنف الواحد من تلك الأصناف أكملهم في هذه الصفات ، ثم في ذلك [ الصنف] يوجد أشخاص كثيرون إلا أنه يحصل فيهم شخص واحد هو أكمل أولئك الأشخاص ، وحينئذ يكون ذلك الشخص هو أكمل الأشخاص الموجودين في عالم الدنيا ، وهو المسمى عند أهل التصوف بقطب العالم . وفي لسان الشيعة بالإمام المعصوم . ثم هؤلاء الأفاضل الذين لا يوجد منهم في الدور الواحد إلا الفرد الواحد ، إذا قوبل بعضهم بالبعض ، فسيوجد في كل ألف سنة أو أقل أو أكثر : شخص واحد هو رئيسهم الأكبر ، وإمامهم الأعظم ، وذلك هو النبي الكامل صاحب الوحي والتنزيل . ولما عرفتك (۳) هذه المراتب في عالم الجسمانيات ، فاعرف مثله في عالم الروحانيات : فالموجودات الروحانية المجردة عن علائق الأجسام كثيرة ومختلفة الدرجات بحسب الكمال (۱) والنقصان ، ولكنهم بأسرهم مشتركون في كونهم بأسرهم أكمل من جنس الإنس ومعشر البشر في الصفات الثلاث المذكورة أعني الاستغناء والعلم والقدرة ، فإن الأرواح البشرية [ بالنسبة إلى تلك الأرواح كالقطرة بالنسبة إلى البحر ، والشعلة بالنسبة إلى الشمس ، وكما أن الأرواح البشرية ] وإن كانت كثيرة جداً إلا أنه لابد ، وأن يوجد فيهم شخص واحد كالرئيس المطلق لهم في الكمالات الروحانية ، بحيث يكونون محتاجين إليه في الأستكمال ، ويكون هو غنياً عنهم. وكذلك الموجودات الروحانية، وإن اختلفت درجاتهم وتفاوتت مراتبهم فإنه لابد وأن الموجودات الروحانية ، وإن اختلفت درجاتهم وتفاوتت مراتبهم فإنه لابد وأن يوجد فيهم موجود هو أكمل من كل الروحانيات في صفة الاستغناء ، والعلم ، والقدرة . ومتى كان الأمر كذلك ، فإنه يكون هو غنياً عن كل الروحانيات ، وكلهم يكونون محتاجين إليه . فقد ثبت أن الجسمانيات محتاجة إلى الروحانيات ، وثبت أن جميع الروحانيات محتاجة إلى ذلك الواحد في جميع الكمالات ، وأنه غنى عنهم في جميع الكمالات ، وعند هذا يظهر أن ذلك الواحد يكون مستولياً على جميع الروحانيات ، وعلى جميع الجسمانيات ، وكل من سواه يكون محتاجاً إليه في وجوده . أما هو فإنه يكون غنياً عن كل ما سواه في كمالات وجوده ، وفي جميع وجوده ، وفي كل كمالات وجوده. وذلك الموجود هو الله تعالى
Whoever has more corporeality is lower and further from perfection. Then when we reflected on defining the attributes of perfection, we found them confined to three kinds: self-sufficiency (al-istighnā'), knowledge (al-ʿilm), and power (al-qudra). Then it is known that these three attributes are not acquired by man in a perfect way, but rather are acquired by him only to the measure of human strength and human capacity. So we observe that the types of the people of the world, even if they are many, yet (1) the one type among those types is the most perfect of them in these attributes. Then within that [type] many individuals exist, yet among them occurs one individual who is the most perfect of those individuals. Then that individual is the most perfect of individuals existing in the lower world, and he is called by the people of Sufism the Pole of the World, and in the language of the Shia the Infallible Imam. Then these excellent ones, of whom only one individual exists in each cycle, when some are compared with others, there will be found in every thousand years or less or more: one individual who is their greatest chief and their supreme leader, and that is the perfect prophet, the possessor of revelation and scripture. And when I have acquainted you (3) with these ranks in the world of physical things, know the like in the world of spiritual things: the spiritual existents abstracted from bodily attachments are many and varied in degrees according to perfection (1) and deficiency, but they all share in that they are all more perfect than the human species and the company of humans in the three mentioned attributes, namely self-sufficiency, knowledge, and power. For the human souls [relative to those souls are like a drop relative to the sea, and a flame relative to the sun, and just as the human souls] even if they are very many, yet necessarily there exists among them one individual who is the absolute chief for them in spiritual perfections, such that they are in need of him for perfection, and he is independent of them. Likewise the spiritual existents, even if their degrees differ and their ranks vary, necessarily there exists among them an existent who is more perfect than all the spiritual beings in the attribute of self-sufficiency, knowledge, and power. And when the matter is so, then he is independent of all spiritual beings, and all of them are in need of him. Thus it has been established that the physical things are in need of the spiritual things, and it is established that all the spiritual things are in need of that one in all perfections, and that he is independent of them in all perfections. And at this point it becomes clear that that one is dominant over all spiritual things and over all physical things, and everyone other than him is in need of him for their existence. As for him, he is independent of everything other than him in the perfections of his existence, and in all his existence, and in all the perfections of his existence. And that existent is God, exalted.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the existence of God based on the hierarchy of perfection observable in both physical and spiritual beings. The author begins by stating a principle: the more corporeal a being is, the lower and further from perfection it is. Then he specifies the three attributes of perfection: self-sufficiency, knowledge, and power. These are not perfectly attained by humans; they only have them in limited measure. Observing the world, we see that among the many types of people, one type is most perfect in these attributes, and within that type, one individual is the most perfect. This individual is the most perfect in the lower world, called the 'Pole' by Sufis and the 'Infallible Imam' by Shia. Among such excellent ones across time, there is one supreme chief, the perfect prophet. Having established this hierarchy in the physical world, the author asks us to analogously consider the spiritual world. Spiritual beings (disembodied souls) are many and vary in perfection, but they are all more perfect than humans in the three attributes. Just as among human souls there is a chief who is independent and others depend on him, so among spiritual beings there must be one who is most perfect in self-sufficiency, knowledge, and power. This being is independent of all, and all are dependent on him. Consequently, physical things depend on spiritual things, and all spiritual things depend on that one. This one is dominant over all physical and spiritual things; everything else needs him for existence, while he is self-sufficient in all aspects. That existent is God.

Key Terms

الروحانيات
صفات الكمال
الاستغناء
العلم
القدرة
قطب العالم
الإمام المعصوم
النبي الكامل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the proof is purely empirical, relying only on observation of human hierarchy.
Correction: The proof uses observation only as a starting point; it then applies a metaphysical principle that an infinite regress is impossible, requiring a self-sufficient being that is the source of all perfection.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the three attributes of perfection?
A) Self-sufficiency, knowledge, and power
B) Life, knowledge, and will
C) Power, justice, and mercy
D) Eternity, power, and wisdom

Key Takeaway
The hierarchy of perfection in both physical and spiritual beings logically requires a single, absolutely perfect being who is self-sufficient and upon whom all depend; that being is God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading how self-sufficiency, knowledge, and power are the perfect attributes that belong to God alone, ask yourself: in which area of your life do you pretend to be self-sufficient, only to later realize your deep need for God? Will you confess that need to Him today and ask Him to supply it?
?
The most perfect human still depends on God. Whom do you look up to as a model of perfection—a scholar, a parent, a leader? Do you ever treat them as if they were independent of God, forgetting that their perfection is a gift not an essence? How can you honor them without falling into that subtle idolatry?
?
In this hierarchy, every being is in need of another, culminating in God who is independent. What is the one thing you are most afraid of losing your 'independence' over—your wealth, reputation, health, or relationships? Can you honestly say today that you are willing to depend on God for that very thing, even if it means losing it?

The Relative Perfection of Spiritual Beings and God's Majesty
A four-step chain of comparisons showing relative perfection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hierarchical comparison of spiritual beings—from human souls to the highest angels—and how all are as nothing before God's majesty.

Core Idea
Even the highest spirits are like nothing before God's majesty.

This passage presents a subtle point that clarifies the relative degrees of perfection among different orders of spiritual beings. It begins with the soul of the Pole, the most perfect human, then compares all prophets and saints to angels, and ultimately contrasts all creation with God. This chain of comparisons emphasizes the absolute transcendence of God.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for its flow and key terms. Then read the translation.
Notice the progression: humans, Pole, angels, high holy spirits, God.
2
Identify the four levels of comparison
The passage makes four sequential comparisons. Identify each pair and the metaphor used.
The metaphors shift from drops/flames to atoms to nothingness.
3
Understand the purpose of the chain
Ask why the author builds this chain. It serves to show the relative insignificance of all creation before God.
The final comparison uses 'nothingness' – the strongest term.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider how this passage reinforces tawhid and God's absolute perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ههنا يظهر دقيقة شريفة ، وهي ان جميع الأرواح البشرية بالنسبة إلى روح الشخص الذي هو قطب العالم ، كالقطرة بالنسبة إلى البحر ، وكالشعلة بالنسبة إلى الشمس . ثم ثبت أن أرواح جميع الأقطاب والأولياء والأنبياء بالنسبة إلى الأرواح الملكية القدسية، كالذرات والهباءات . ثم إن الأرواح الملكية لا تزال متزايدة في الكمال والرفعة والجلال ، حتى تنتهي إلى الأرواح العالية المقدسة ثم إن جميع تلك الروحانيات بالنسبة إلى جلال الله ، كالعدم فإنـا بينا
Then here appears a noble subtle point, which is that all human souls relative to the soul of the person who is the Pole of the World are like a drop relative to the sea, and like a flame relative to the sun. Then it is established that the souls of all the poles, saints, and prophets relative to the holy angelic spirits are like atoms and particles. Then the angelic spirits continuously increase in perfection, loftiness, and majesty until they end at the high holy spirits. Then all those spiritual beings relative to the majesty of God are like nothingness, for we have explained.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage presents a subtle point (dakiqa sharifa) that further clarifies the relative degrees of perfection among different orders of spiritual beings in relation to God. First, the author states that all human souls, even the soul of the Pole (the most perfect human), are like a drop compared to the sea and a flame compared to the sun when compared to the soul of the Pole. Then he says that the souls of all poles, saints, and prophets are like atoms and dust particles relative to the holy angelic spirits. The angelic spirits themselves continuously increase in perfection, loftiness, and majesty until they reach the highest holy spirits. Finally, all these spiritual beings, even the highest angels, are like nothingness in comparison to the majesty of God. The author ends by indicating that this has been explained (presumably in earlier arguments).

Key Terms
دقيقة شريفة
قطب العالم
الأرواح الملكية القدسية
الأرواح العالية المقدسة
جلال الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Pole or highest angels are comparable to God in perfection.
Correction: The passage shows that even the highest spirits are as nothing before God's majesty, emphasizing absolute divine transcendence.

Checkpoint
According to the subtle point, how are all spiritual beings (including angelic spirits) compared to the majesty of God?
A) Like a drop to the sea
B) Like atoms and particles
C) Like nothingness (al-ʿadam)
D) Like a flame to the sun

Key Takeaway
Everything in creation, no matter how exalted, is as nothing compared to the majesty of God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the most perfect saints and angels are nothing before God's majesty, what does that reveal about your own sense of pride or self-importance? In what specific situation this week can you practice genuine humility in your worship or interactions?
?
The passage describes a chain of perfection leading up to God. Where do you honestly place yourself on that chain? In what areas of your life do you still act as if you are the center of the universe, and what step can you take today to realign your focus toward God alone?
?
Even the high holy spirits are like nothingness before God. How should this truth change the way you view your achievements and failures? What would it mean for you to submit every part of your life—your work, relationships, and private thoughts—to God's majesty, starting right now?

Proof from the Hierarchy of Spiritual Beings
Proof of God from hierarchy of spiritual beings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hierarchy of spiritual beings necessitates a single highest perfect being, which is God.

Core Idea
The hierarchy of perfections in spiritual beings points to one ultimate source.

This lesson presents a fascinating argument for God's existence based on the inherent hierarchy among spiritual beings. By observing the need for a pinnacle in any hierarchy of perfections, we can infer the existence of a single most perfect being upon whom all else depends.

Guided Path
1
Understand spiritual beings and their attributes
Read the passage carefully. Notice that spiritual beings are described as more perfect than humans in three attributes: self-sufficiency, knowledge, and power.
These attributes are key to the argument.
2
Analogy with human souls
The author draws an analogy: among human souls, despite their numbers, there must be one absolute leader who is more perfect and upon whom others depend.
Think of a hierarchy needing a top.
3
Extend the analogy to all spiritual beings
Similarly, among all spiritual beings, there must be one most perfect being who is independent and the source of perfection for all others.
This is the core inference.
4
Identify the conclusion
The passage concludes that this being has dominion over all and is God, the Exalted.
This is the ultimate conclusion of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدرجات بحسب الكمال والنقصان، ولكنهم بأسرهم مشتركون في كونهم بأسرهم أكمل من جنس الإنس ومعشر البشر في الصفات الثلاث المذكورة أعني الاستغناء والعلم والقدرة، فإن الأرواح البشرية [ بالنسبة إلى تلك الأرواح كالقطرة بالنسبة إلى البحر، والشعلة بالنسبة إلى الشمس، وكما أن الأرواح البشرية ] وإن كانت كثيرة جداً إلا أنه لابد وأن يوجد فيهم شخص واحد كالرئيس المطلق لهم في الكمالات الروحانية، بحيث يكونون محتاجين إليه في الأستكمال، ويكون هو غنياً عنهم. وكذلك الموجودات الروحانية، وإن اختلفت درجاتهم وتفاوتت مراتبهم فإنه لابد وأن يوجد فيهم موجود هو أكمل من كل الروحانيات في صفة الاستغناء، والعلم، والقدرة. ومتى كان الأمر كذلك، فإنه يكون هو غنياً عن كل الروحانيات، وكلهم يكونون محتاجين إليه. فقد ثبت أن الجسمانيات محتاجة إلى الروحانيات، وثبت أن جميع الروحانيات محتاجة إلى ذلك الواحد في جميع الكمالات، وأنه غنى عنهم في جميع الكمالات، وعند هذا يظهر أن ذلك الواحد يكون مستولياً على جميع الروحانيات، وعلى جميع الجسمانيات، وكل من سواه يكون محتاجاً إليه في وجوده. أما هو فإنه يكون غنياً عن كل ما سواه في كمالات وجوده، وفي جميع وجوده، وفي كل كمالات وجوده. وذلك الموجود هو الله تعالى.
Degrees are according to perfection and deficiency, but they all share in being more perfect than the human race and mankind in the three mentioned attributes: self-sufficiency, knowledge, and power. For human souls [compared to those souls are like a drop compared to the sea, and a flame compared to the sun, and just as human souls] although they are very numerous, it is necessary that among them there be one person like the absolute leader for them in spiritual perfections, such that they are in need of him for completion, and he is independent of them. Likewise, the spiritual existents, although their degrees differ and their ranks vary, it is necessary that among them there exist an existent that is more perfect than all spiritual beings in the attribute of self-sufficiency, knowledge, and power. When this is the case, then he is independent of all spiritual beings, and all of them are in need of him. Thus it is established that corporeal beings are in need of spiritual beings, and it is established that all spiritual beings are in need of that One in all perfections, and that He is independent of them in all perfections. At this point it becomes apparent that that One has dominion over all spiritual beings and over all corporeal beings, and everyone other than Him is in need of Him for their existence. As for Him, He is independent of everything other than Him in the perfections of His existence, in all His existence, and in every perfection of His existence. That Existent is God the Exalted.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the existence of God (Allah) as the highest and most perfect being, based on the hierarchy of spiritual beings. The author begins by stating that spiritual beings (روحانيات) differ in degrees of perfection and deficiency, but they all share the characteristic of being more perfect than humans in three attributes: self-sufficiency (استغناء), knowledge (علم), and power (قدرة). Among human souls, despite their great number, there must be one perfect person who is the absolute leader (الرئيس المطلق) in spiritual perfections, upon whom all others depend for completion, while he is independent of them. Similarly, among spiritual existents, despite their varying degrees, there must be one existent that is the most perfect in those three attributes. This being is independent of all other spiritual beings, and all are in need of Him. The author then concludes that corporeal beings (جسمانيات) depend on spiritual beings, and all spiritual beings depend on that One. This One has dominion over all, and everything else needs Him for existence, while He is independent in all aspects. That existent is God the Exalted.

Key Terms

جسمانيات
استغناء
علم
قدرة
الرئيس المطلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is just another version of the cosmological argument from contingency.
Correction: It is specifically based on the hierarchy of perfections among spiritual beings, not on contingency or causation of existence itself.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what attributes do all spiritual beings share that make them more perfect than humans?
A) Life, power, will
B) Self-sufficiency, knowledge, power
C) Eternity, omnipotence, wisdom
D) Mercy, justice, truth

Key Takeaway
The hierarchy of perfections in spiritual beings necessitates a single perfect independent being, who is God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your life, who or what do you treat as the ultimate source of spiritual perfection? Does your heart lean on any created being—whether a teacher, saint, or angel—as though they are independent of God? How does this passage expose that tendency and call you to turn back to God alone?
?
You have just read that even the highest spiritual beings are in need of God for their existence and perfections. Are you living as if that is true? Search your daily habits: where do you act as if you can achieve perfection on your own, or as if someone else’s approval is your ultimate goal? Commit to one specific change that redirects your reliance from creatures to the Creator.
?
The analogy of human souls needing an absolute leader mirrors our dependence on God. Do you more often run to human leaders (spiritual guides, mentors) for what only God can give? What would it look like for you to seek completion directly from God while still honoring those He placed as means? Ask yourself honestly: who holds the throne of your heart?
