The Proof of Mutual Exclusion (Burhan al-Tamānu')
The author presents and explains the proof of mutual exclusion for God's unity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the structure and logical force of the proof of mutual exclusion for God's unity.

Core Idea
Two omnipotent gods cannot coexist; the universe itself proves that only One is possible.

This lesson unpacks one of the most powerful rational arguments for tawheed—the proof of mutual exclusion (burhan al-tamānu'). The argument proceeds by examining what would happen if there were two gods, and shows that every possibility leads to an impossibility or contradiction. The proof is rooted in the Quranic verse (21:22) and is given a rigorous logical form by the theologians.

Guided Path
1
Read and observe the passage
Read the Arabic source and its English translation carefully. Notice how the author begins with a Quranic verse and then presents a logical analysis.
The proof is called 'burhan al-tamānu'' because it shows that two gods would mutually exclude each other.
2
Identify the three scenarios
The author lists three possibilities regarding the power and will of two supposed gods. Find these three cases in the text.
3
Analyze each scenario's outcome
For each of the three cases, understand why the author says it leads to impossibility or contradiction. Consider why the first case is impossible, the second implies incapability, and the third denies godhood.
This logical trilemma is the core of the proof.
4
Examine the deeper reasoning
After the trilemma, the author provides additional arguments about the impossibility of two eternal beings with absolute perfection. Notice how he links twoness with distinction and the inability to maintain a single order.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand how this proof establishes that only one God can exist, and that the observed order and perfection of the universe confirm this.
The proof is both scriptural and rational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويذكر الآية القرآنية : ( لو كان فيهما آلهة إلا الله لفسدتا ) [الأنبياء ٢٢] ويقول : لن يقوم على ثبوت الوحدانية برهان أقوى من هذا البرهان. وهو برهان التمانع ، كما يسميه المتكلمون وأحسن من يشرحه هكذا . لا يخلو إما أن يكون قدرة كل واحد منهما وإرادته كافية في وجود العالم أو لا شيء منها كاف ، أو أحدهما كاف فقط. وعلى الأول يلزم اجتماع المؤثرين التامين على معلول واحد . وهو محال . وعلى الثاني يلزم عجزهما، لأنها لا يمكن لهما التأثير إلا باشتراك الآخر . وعلى الثالث ألا يكون الآخر خالقا، فلا يكون إلها . وصواب الأمر : إن وجود المين سرمديين مستحيل . وإن بلوغ الكمال المطلق في صفة من الصفات يمنع بلوغ كمال مطلق آخر في تلك الصفة، وان الأثنينية و لا تتحقق في موجدين كلاهما يلا بداية ولا نهاية ولا حدود ولا فروق . وكلاهما يريد ما يريده الآخر، ويقدر ما يقدره، ويعمل ما يعمله في كل حال، وفي كل صغير وكبير . فهذان وجود واحد وليسا بوجودين . فإذا كانا اثنين لم يكونا إلا متمايزين متغايرين. فلا ينتظم على هذا التمايز والتغاير نظام واحد . وإذا كانا هما كاملين فالمخلوقات ناقصة، ولا يكون تدبير المخلوق الناقص على وجه واحد، بل على وجوه .
And he mentions the Quranic verse: (If there were in them [the heavens and the earth] gods besides Allah, they would have been ruined) [Al-Anbiya 22]. And he says: There will not stand a proof stronger than this proof for establishing unity. And it is the proof of mutual exclusion (burhan al-tamānu'), as the theologians call it, and the best way to explain it is as follows: It is inevitably either that each one's power and will are sufficient for the existence of the world, or none of them is sufficient, or only one of them is sufficient. On the first, it necessitates the concurrence of two full agents on one effect, which is impossible. On the second, it necessitates their incapability, because neither can effect except through the participation of the other. On the third, the other would not be a creator, and thus would not be a god. And the correct matter is: The existence of two eternal beings is impossible. And the attainment of absolute perfection in an attribute prevents another absolute perfection from attaining that same attribute. And twoness is not realized in two existents, both without beginning, without end, without limits, and without differences. And each wills what the other wills, and determines what the other determines, and does what the other does in every state, in every small and large matter. So these two are one existence, not two existences. If they are two, they are only distinct and different. Then upon this distinctness and difference, a single order cannot be established. And if they are both perfect, then created things are imperfect, and the management of the imperfect created thing is not upon one single way, but upon multiple ways.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage presents and explains the proof of mutual exclusion (burhan al-tamānu') for the unity of God. The author first cites the Quranic verse (21:22) which states that if there were multiple gods, the heavens and earth would be ruined. He then asserts that no proof stronger than this exists for establishing tawheed, and that the theologians call it 'burhan al-tamānu'. He explains it through a logical breakdown of possibilities regarding two supposed gods: either both are fully capable of creating the world, or neither is, or only one is. On the first scenario, two fully effective agents acting on one effect is impossible (this would entail concurrence of two perfect causes on one effect). On the second, both would be incapable, as each needs the other's participation. On the third, the other would not be a creator, hence not a god. The author then gives the correct view: the existence of two eternal beings is impossible because absolute perfection in an attribute prevents another being from possessing that same absolute perfection. Furthermore, twoness cannot be realized in two beings that are both eternal, limitless, and without differences; if they are truly two, they must be distinct and different, but then a single coherent order cannot be maintained. If both are perfect, then the imperfect creation cannot be managed in a single way, but only in multiple ways, which contradicts the notion of a single ordered universe.

Key Terms
برهان التمانع
الوحدانية
آلهة
خالق
إله
معلول
مؤثرين تامين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the proof of mutual exclusion is purely scriptural and not rational.
Correction: The author presents a logical trilemma and additional reasoning that is independent of revelation, making it a rational proof as well.

Checkpoint
According to the proof of mutual exclusion, what is the consequence if both supposed gods have sufficient power and will to create the world?
A) The world would be created in a perfect manner.
B) It would require the concurrence of two full agents on one effect, which is impossible.
C) Both gods would be incapable.
D) Only one god would be the creator.

Key Takeaway
The proof of mutual exclusion shows that the existence of more than one God is logically impossible, because any scenario of multiple gods leads to contradiction or failure.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the existence of two gods is logically impossible, then what does it say about your heart when you fear or hope in anything or anyone as if they share Allah's power? In what areas of your life do you act as if there is a second 'god' controlling outcomes?
?
The proof shows that absolute perfection can only belong to One. Where in your life do you still seek perfection from created things—people, status, possessions—knowing they are imperfect? Will you repent and turn to the Only Perfect One today?
?
When you face a situation where your desires conflict with Allah's command, which 'will' do you follow? Do you truly believe that only His will should prevail, even when it costs you? What concrete step will you take tonight to submit your will to His?

Three Interpretations of 'Necessary of Existence in Itself'
Enumeration and critique of three interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three interpretations of 'necessary of existence in itself' and why the author rejects those based on negative concepts.

Core Idea
The true meaning of 'necessary of existence' is a positive attribute of self-subsistence.

Before we can discuss what it means for Allah to be necessary of existence, we must clarify the term itself. The author presents three possible interpretations, but he shows that only one captures the full meaning. This lesson will help you distinguish between a positive attribute and merely negative descriptions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Notice that the author lists three interpretations and then discusses their differences.
The text is incomplete at the end, but the key ideas are present.
2
Identify the three interpretations
List the three interpretations from the passage. The first: 'deserves existence from its own self.' The second: 'does not accept non-existence.' The third: 'does not depend on a separate cause.'
These are distinct meanings.
3
Understand positive vs. negative
The author says the first interpretation is a positive concept, while the other two are negative. Ask yourself: Why would a negative description be insufficient to capture what 'necessary of existence' truly means?
A positive concept affirms something about the essence; a negative concept only denies something.
4
Consider the critique of the second interpretation
The author argues that saying 'does not accept non-existence' is problematic because existence itself does not accept non-existence, yet existence is not necessary in itself. This shows the danger of using purely negative definitions.

المسألة الأولى
البحث عن معنى قولنا: إنه واجب الوجود لذاته
اعلم. أنه يمكن تفسيره بأمور ثلاثة: أحدها: أنه الذي يستحق الوجود من ذاته. وثانيها: أنه الذي لا يقبل العلم، أو أنه الذي لا يصح عليه العدم. وثالثها: أنه الذي لا يتوقف وجوده على سبب منفصل فهذه وجوه ثلاثة مغايرة. ولتذكر الفرق بين هذه المفهومات الثلاثة:
أما قولنا: إنه الذي يستحق الوجود من ذاته. فهذا مفهوم ثبوتي. وهو يفيد كون ذاته علة لوجود نفسه. وأما الوجهان الآخران. وهما قولنا: إنه لا يقبل العدم، أو إنه الذي يستغني عن السبب. فمفهومان سلبيان (1).
ثم نقول: قولنا: واجب الوجود لذاته هو الذي لا يقبل العدم [من حيث هو هو. فيه بحث. وذلك لأن الوجود من حيث إنه وجود، لا يقبل العدم] (2) البتة، مع أن. مسمى الوجود، ليس واجبا لذاته.
وأما قولنا: إن واجب الوجود لذاته، هو الذي لا يكون وجوده معللا بسبب منفصل، فهذا أيضا فيه نظر. لأن أقسام الموجودات، بحسب التقيم
The First Issue: Inquiry into the meaning of our statement: He is necessary of existence in Himself. Know that it can be interpreted by three matters: One of them: that He is the one who deserves existence from His own self. The second: that He is the one who does not accept non-existence, or that non-existence is not valid for Him. The third: that He is the one whose existence does not depend on a separate cause. So these are three different aspects. And to mention the difference between these three concepts: As for our statement: He is the one who deserves existence from His own self – this is a positive concept. And it indicates that His essence is the cause of His own existence. As for the other two aspects, namely our statement: He does not accept non-existence, or He is the one who is independent of the cause – they are two negative concepts. Then we say: Our statement: the necessary of existence in Himself is the one who does not accept non-existence [insofar as it is itself. There is an investigation in it. That is because existence insofar as it is existence does not accept non-existence] at all, even though the meaning of existence is not necessary in itself. And as for our statement: the necessary of existence in Himself is the one whose existence is not caused by a separate cause – this also has some consideration. Because the divisions of existents, according to the division...
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a definition and critical examination. The author begins by stating that the term 'necessary of existence in Himself' (واجب الوجود لذاته) can be interpreted in three ways. First, it means that which deserves existence from its own essence. Second, it means that which does not accept non-existence, or that non-existence is not valid for it. Third, it means that whose existence does not depend on a separate cause. These three interpretations are distinct. The author then explains the difference: the first is a positive concept (مفهوم ثبوتي), indicating that the essence is the cause of its own existence. The other two are negative concepts (مفهومان سلبيان). Then the author critiques the second interpretation: saying that the necessary of existence is that which does not accept non-existence is problematic because existence as such does not accept non-existence, yet existence is not necessary in itself. The third interpretation is also problematic because the divisions of existents according to... (the text breaks off). The author is thus refining the definition by showing that the negative interpretations are insufficient or lead to issues.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All three interpretations are equivalent ways of saying the same thing.
Correction: The author explicitly states they are different, and that the first is positive while the other two are negative. Moreover, the negative ones are problematic.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The correct understanding of 'necessary of existence in itself' is a positive concept: the essence is the cause of its own existence, not merely the absence of non-existence or dependence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often define God by what He is not (e.g., 'not limited,' 'not dependent'). After studying this lesson, do you see how relying only on negative definitions can fail to acknowledge the full reality of His existence? Will you now strive to affirm His perfect attributes positively, even when your mind struggles?
?
When you say 'Allah is necessary of existence,' have you truly pondered that His essence is the very cause of His existence, while you are utterly dependent? Does this realization humble you and demand that you live in constant awareness of your contingency?
?
The author critiques the definition 'does not accept non-existence' because existence itself does not accept non-existence. Have you ever mistakenly thought that the impossibility of God's non-existence is what makes Him God, rather than His intrinsic perfection? How can you correct this in your own heart and worship?

Three Interpretations of Necessary Existence
Razi enumerates three interpretations of 'necessary existence' and distinguishes positive from negative concepts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three ways Razi interprets 'necessary of existence in itself' and how he distinguishes positive from negative definitions.

Core Idea
Razi shows that 'necessary existence' can be defined positively or negatively, with only one being genuinely positive.

Razi begins by clarifying the very term 'necessary of existence in itself,' which is central to arguments for God's existence. He offers three possible interpretations, then highlights a crucial difference: the first is a positive concept, while the other two are negative. This sets the stage for evaluating which definition is truly adequate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its English translation. Notice the three definitions listed.
The passage is short but packed with meaning.
2
Identify the three interpretations
List the three interpretations as presented by Razi. Observe that the second is given in two phrasings.
The second interpretation is stated as 'does not accept non-existence' or 'non-existence is not valid for Him'.
3
Distinguish positive from negative
Razi classifies the first as positive (thubuti) and the other two as negative (salbi). Reflect on why the first is considered positive.
The first affirms a causal relationship; the others negate something.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الأولى
البحث عن معنى قولنا: إنه واجب الوجود لذاته
اعلم . أنه يمكن تفسيره بأمور ثلاثة : أحدها: أنه الذي يستحق الوجود من ذاته . وثانيها : أنه الذي لا يقبل العلم، أو أنه الذي لا يصح عليه العدم . وثالثها : أنه الذي لا يتوقف وجوده على سبب منفصل فهذه وجوه ثلاثة مغايرة . ولتذكر الفرق بين هذه المفهومات الثلاثة :
أما قولنا : إنه الذي يستحق الوجود من ذاته. فهذا مفهوم ثبوتي . وهو يفيد كون ذاته علة لوجود نفسه . وأما الوجهان الآخران . وهما قولنا : إنه لا يقبل العدم ، أو إنه الذي يستغني عن السبب . فمفهومان سلبيان (۱) .
The First Question: Investigation into the meaning of our statement: He is necessary of existence in itself. Know that it can be interpreted in three ways: First: that He is the one who deserves existence from Himself. Second: that He is the one who does not accept non-existence, or that He is the one for whom non-existence is not valid. Third: that He is the one whose existence does not depend on a separate cause. So these are three different aspects. And let us remember the difference between these three concepts: As for our statement: He is the one who deserves existence from Himself, this is a positive concept. It indicates that His essence is the cause of His own existence. As for the other two aspects, namely our statement: He does not accept non-existence, or He is the one who is independent of the cause, they are two negative concepts (1).
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'necessary of existence in itself' (واجب الوجود لذاته) by presenting three possible interpretations. The author begins by stating that the meaning can be explained in three ways. First: He is the one who deserves existence from His own essence, meaning that existence is due to Him inherently. Second: He is the one who does not admit non-existence, i.e., His existence is eternal and cannot cease. Third: He is the one whose existence does not depend on any separate cause. The author then clarifies that these three are distinct concepts. He further distinguishes between them: the first interpretation is a positive concept (مفهوم ثبوتي) because it affirms that His essence is the cause of His existence. The second and third interpretations are negative concepts (مفهومان سلبيان) because they negate non-existence or dependence on a cause. This sets the stage for critiquing the adequacy of the negative definitions.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود لذاته
مفهوم ثبوتي
مفهوم سلبي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think all three definitions are equivalent or all are positive.
Correction: Razi explicitly states that the first is a positive concept (مفهوم ثبوتي) and the other two are negative concepts (مفهومان سلبيان), showing they are distinct in nature.

Checkpoint

B) Two; they are negative concepts
C) Three; they are negative concepts

Key Takeaway
The first interpretation of 'necessary existence' is positive (affirming a cause), while the other two are negative (denying non-existence or dependence).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah is necessary of existence', do you truly affirm a positive necessity – that He deserves existence from Himself – or are you merely negating His non-existence? Examine your inner certainty: is it rooted in a positive conviction of His intrinsic deserving, or just an intellectual rejection of His absence? How would your reliance on Him change if you moved from the second to the first?
?
If Allah's existence depends on no cause, then your entire existence depends entirely on Him. Do you live as if this is true? In what specific area of your life have you been acting as if some part of your existence or success depends on a cause other than Allah? Commit today to tracing one such false dependence back to its root and replacing it with trust in the Self-Sufficient.
?
Razi calls the first concept 'positive' because it affirms that Allah's essence is the cause of His own existence. But does your heart actually rest in that truth? Or do you find yourself paying lip service while secretly feeling that Allah's existence is a 'given' without emotional weight? Spend one minute in silent contemplation of the phrase 'He deserves existence from Himself' – not as a fact, but as a reality that demands your whole being.

Critique of the Second Interpretation
Razi critiques the definition of necessary existence as 'not accepting non-existence'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why defining necessary existence as 'not accepting non-existence' is insufficient, and how that definition inadvertently applies to existence itself.

Core Idea
Defining necessity as 'does not accept non-existence' is too broad — even contingent existence resists non-existence.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi examines a proposed definition of the Necessary Being: 'that which does not admit non-existence.' He finds it problematic because existence itself, in its abstract sense, never admits non-existence. Yet existence is not inherently necessary. This critique shows why negative definitions alone cannot capture the uniqueness of the Necessary Being.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal translation. Notice the structure: a statement, then a problem, then an explanation.
The bracketed phrase 'من حيث هو هو' is part of the definition being critiqued.
2
Identify the definition being critiqued
Find the definition: 'واجب الوجود لذاته هو الذي لا يقبل العدم' (Necessary of existence in itself is the one that does not accept non-existence). This is the second interpretation under scrutiny.
3
Understand the problem
The author points out that existence as such (الوجود من حيث هو وجود) also does not accept non-existence. So the definition applies to all existence, not just the Necessary.
Contingent beings exist, but they are not necessary; they could cease to exist.
4
Reflect on the consequence
Consider why this definition fails: it does not distinguish the Necessary Being from other existents. A proper definition must be exclusive.
This lesson shows the importance of precision in theological definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : قولنا : واجب الوجود لذاته هو الذي لا يقبل العدم [من حيث هو هو . فيه بحث . وذلك لأن الوجود من حيث إنه وجود ، لا يقبل العدم ] (٢) البتة ، مع أن . مسمى الوجود ، ليس واجبا لذاته .
Then we say: Our statement: Necessary of existence in itself is the one that does not accept non-existence [insofar as it is itself]. This requires examination. That is because existence insofar as it is existence does not accept non-existence at all, even though the meaning of existence is not necessary in itself.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage critiques the second interpretation, which defines necessary existence as 'that which does not accept non-existence'. The author points out a problem: existence as such (الوجود من حيث هو وجود) never accepts non-existence, because existence is the opposite of non-existence. But this does not mean that everything that exists is necessary in itself. For example, contingent beings exist but are not necessary; they could cease to exist. Therefore, the definition is too broad and does not uniquely identify the Necessary Being. The author implies that a proper definition must go beyond this negative characterization.

Key Terms
لا يقبل العدم
الوجود من حيث هو وجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The definition 'does not accept non-existence' uniquely identifies the Necessary Being.
Correction: Existence itself does not accept non-existence, but not everything that exists is necessary; therefore the definition is too broad.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the second interpretation?
A) Because it is a positive concept
B) Because existence as such does not accept non-existence, yet not every existent is necessary
C) Because it is too specific
D) Because it depends on a separate cause

Key Takeaway
Defining necessary existence negatively as 'not accepting non-existence' is insufficient because it applies to existence itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever defined Allah's necessity in terms that could also apply to His creation—like simply 'He exists forever'? What distinguishes your understanding from the existence of contingent things?
?
If your concept of Allah's existence is merely that 'He does not cease to exist', how does that differ from the permanence of the universe? What must you add to your understanding to truly grasp His necessity?
